    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13963238851592392844">"<i>Die Entdeckung der Langsamkeit</i>" ist auf den ersten Blick zugleich ein Seefahrerroman, ein Roman über das Abenteuer und die Sehnsucht danach und ein Entwicklungsroman. Doch hat Sten Nadolny die Biographie des englischen Seefahrers und Nordpolforschers John Franklin (1786-1847) zu einer subtilen Studie über die Zeit umgeschrieben: die Langsamkeit als eine Kunst, dem Rhythmu</span>
  <span id="freeText13963238851592392844" style="display:none">"<i>Die Entdeckung der Langsamkeit</i>" ist auf den ersten Blick zugleich ein Seefahrerroman, ein Roman über das Abenteuer und die Sehnsucht danach und ein Entwicklungsroman. Doch hat Sten Nadolny die Biographie des englischen Seefahrers und Nordpolforschers John Franklin (1786-1847) zu einer subtilen Studie über die Zeit umgeschrieben: die Langsamkeit als eine Kunst, dem Rhythmus des Lebens Sinn zu verleihen. Wie bei einem Palimpsest erscheint hinter den Sätzen eine andere Schrift, hinter der Prägnanz und Redlichkeit der Aufklärung verbergen sich Humor und Traurigkeit der Romantik.<br /><br />Von Kindheit an träumt John Franklin davon, zur See zu fahren, obwohl er dafür denkbar ungeeignet ist: Langsam im Sprechen und Denken, langsam in seinen Reaktionen mißt er die Zeit nach eigenen Maßstäben. Zunächst erkennt nur sein Lehrer, daß Johns eigenartige Behinderung auch Vorzüge hat - was er einmal erfaßt hat, das behält er, das Einzigartige, das Detail begreift er besser als andere. John Franklin geht zur Marine, erlebt den Krieg und das Sterben. Beides trifft ihn um so furchtbarer, als er innerhalb des von ihm kaum begriffenen, chaotisch schnellen Geschehens einzelne Vorgänge wie in Zeitlupe ablaufen sieht. Er träumt von friedlicher Entdeckung, will die legendäre Nordwestpassage finden.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13963238851592392844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/846983658" />
    <a title="Jenny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6565711-jenny"><img alt="Jenny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324233459p2/6565711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/846983658?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny" href="/user/show/6565711-jenny">Jenny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9783936384543" href="/book/show/1491048.Die_Entdeckung_der_Langsamkeit">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6565711-jenny?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6565711-jenny?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6565711-jenny?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6565711-jenny?shelf=german">german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6565711-jenny?shelf=sea-books">sea-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6565711-jenny?shelf=travelling">travelling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer846983658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9041415700282813719">Nadolny tells the story of the British Royal Navy Officer and Arctic explorer John Franklin who died in 1847 while attempting to chart and navigate a section of the Northwest Passage in the Canadian Arctic. The historical sources are well studied, but Nadolny has found an own explanation for Franklin's iron will.<br/><br/>John Franklin is slow, very slow. When other children play ball, he holds the cord because he's too slow to catch. The cord however he can hold for hours. This alleged handicap also has </span>
  <span id="freeText9041415700282813719" style="display:none">Nadolny tells the story of the British Royal Navy Officer and Arctic explorer John Franklin who died in 1847 while attempting to chart and navigate a section of the Northwest Passage in the Canadian Arctic. The historical sources are well studied, but Nadolny has found an own explanation for Franklin's iron will.<br /><br />John Franklin is slow, very slow. When other children play ball, he holds the cord because he's too slow to catch. The cord however he can hold for hours. This alleged handicap also has it's benefits. He sees and listens more thouroughly than others, his eyes and ears hold on to every impression for accurate verification before passing the signal on to the brain.<br />John does not lose time, he just uses it differently.<br /><br />Nadolny follows him through his childhood, his loves - lost and kept, his time as navy officer and as governor of Van Diemen's Land in Tasmania. He does so in a slow, deliberated prose, lot's of warmth and subtle wit, making this book many things at once: a historical novel, an adventure novel and a wonderful meditation on time and perception.<br /><br />Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9041415700282813719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="GoldGato" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6401606-goldgato"><img alt="GoldGato" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407995357p2/6401606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2619037187?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="GoldGato" class="user" itemprop="url" name="GoldGato" href="/user/show/6401606-goldgato">GoldGato</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781589880245" href="/book/show/26098.The_Discovery_of_Slowness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6401606-goldgato?shelf=exploration">exploration</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6401606-goldgato?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6401606-goldgato?shelf=maritime">maritime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6401606-goldgato?shelf=winter">winter</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2619037187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6268926220117771762">A superb biographical novel about Sir John Franklin, the British naval explorer who disappeared into the Arctic while trying to determine the Northwest Passage. The title says it all, for it is about a person who is "slow" yet manages to make the world fit within his own limited skill sets.<br/><br/><i>The struggle to find and live by one's own rhythm defines what it is to be human.</i><br/><br/>Franklin's childhood, expounding on his slowness and his father's lack of feeling toward his dull son, leads to a career at sea.</span>
  <span id="freeText6268926220117771762" style="display:none">A superb biographical novel about Sir John Franklin, the British naval explorer who disappeared into the Arctic while trying to determine the Northwest Passage. The title says it all, for it is about a person who is "slow" yet manages to make the world fit within his own limited skill sets.<br /><br /><i>The struggle to find and live by one's own rhythm defines what it is to be human.</i><br /><br />Franklin's childhood, expounding on his slowness and his father's lack of feeling toward his dull son, leads to a career at sea. There, Franklin finds his niche. Slow but patient, he develops navigational skills and learns, in OCD style, every inch of every ship while memorizing commands and his responses. He probably didn't fit in with the normal below-decks bravura of his shipmates, but he turns out to be brave and stolid, mostly because of his slowness.<br /><br /><i>The moral quality of all his acts lay in the length of time they had endured or in their intended duration.</i><br /><br />John Franklin survived shipwrecks and battles and the squalid in-fighting of Tasmania (while governor) to become an admired member of the British navy and then a much admired member of British explorers. It is the detailing of his disastrous expedition to the north of Canada, where men were killed and eaten due to starvation, which really brings this book to life. Although his reputation took a slight hit, the fact that anyone even returned alive from that horror brought even more respect to the graying officer. So when a leader was needed to find the last piece of the Northwest Passage, Franklin was their man. He and his men sailed off into oblivion, until eventual clues to their demise turned up decades later.<br /><br /><i>Who should rule in this world? Which third man among three should tell the other two what to do?</i><br /><br />The Arctic adventurers have always enthralled me and when they recently found one of Franklin's ships, more than 170 years later, it just made his story so much more intriguing. When Sir John Franklin was made the leader of that last journey, he was an old man and overweight, probably not the best fit. Now after reading this historical fiction, I can understand how his firm qualities would have made him the leader they needed. But if that is so, was his patience and slowness one of the reasons the expedition vanished? Could they have left the ice sooner if he could have thought quicker?<br /><br />The translation is perfect, the writing is marvellous. Everything is measured, everything is paced. Even the Nelsonic sea fights seem to pass the reader in slow motion. Franklin is <i>a man who carried a chaos of individual pictures in his head</i>. I'm slow, too. Finally, here's a book which illustrates how some of us eventually catch on to those thoughts that had previously flown by us.<br /><br />I didn't want this book to end.<br /><br />Book Season = Winter (frozen toes, eaten hearts)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6268926220117771762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17863787192672311862">Die Entdeckung der Langsamkeit<br/>By Sten Nadolny<br/><br/>This work is a historical fiction based on the life of Sir John Franklin (1786 - 1847).<br/><br/>Great Britain at the beginning of the nineteenth century.<br/><br/>Historical naval battles at Copenhagen, Trafalgar and New Orleans, John Franklins is engaged in all of them. He sailed on board the ‘’Investigator’ to the coasts of Australia.<br/><br/>He participated in an expedition to the North pole and two Antarctic expeditions before being named Governor of Tasmania where he stays </span>
  <span id="freeText17863787192672311862" style="display:none">Die Entdeckung der Langsamkeit<br />By Sten Nadolny<br /><br />This work is a historical fiction based on the life of Sir John Franklin (1786 - 1847).<br /><br />Great Britain at the beginning of the nineteenth century.<br /><br />Historical naval battles at Copenhagen, Trafalgar and New Orleans, John Franklins is engaged in all of them. He sailed on board the ‘’Investigator’ to the coasts of Australia.<br /><br />He participated in an expedition to the North pole and two Antarctic expeditions before being named Governor of Tasmania where he stays for seven years. <br /><br />In 1845 Sir John was launching the “Franklin Expedition” aiming to discover the Northwest Passage, north of Canada.<br />He was in charge of two ships with 134 men on board, the ‘HMS Erebus’ and ‘HMS Terror’.<br />Their ships got stuck in ice, and none of them survived.<br /><br />This, in a few words, is the real historical background, beautifully and well described in this book.<br /><br />The fictitious part is Franklin’s affliction imagined by the author, which he calls ‘slowness.’<br /><br />Hence the title of the book “The discovery of slowness.”<br /><br />According to the author, Franklin had been born with this anomaly called autistic.<br /><br />He could not react to what his eyes are seeing, speedily, like other people.<br />As a boy, he could not catch a ball. For any questions asked, it had to go around his brain slowly before he could come up with an answer.<br /><br />I am a reader of adventure books of which I have many on my shelves, but not of psychology.<br />I have no patience following up on different conjectures why ‘slowness’ could, in fact, be superior to speed.<br /><br />As for John Franklin to be afflicted with such a handicap, it seems very unlikely.<br />On the contrary, he was a hugely successful man in the circumstances he lived he must have <br />been exceptionally wise, witty, robust, perseverant and intelligent.<br /><br />I am looking forward to finding other books and biographies on John Franklin.<br /></span>

<div id="review_191815225" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/191815225" />
    <a title="Molly Major" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5914964-molly-major"><img alt="Molly Major" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/191815225?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Molly Major" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Molly Major" href="/user/show/5914964-molly-major">Molly Major</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781589880245" href="/book/show/26098.The_Discovery_of_Slowness">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191815225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9617945315050853265">A little known and fine piece of literature is the novel Die Entdeckung der Langsamkeit (The Discovery of Slowness), by Sten Nadolny. The story is a fictionalized account of John Franklin, a historical explorer around the turn of the 19th century. As the protagonist, John Franklin is the most unlikely of adventurers because he is regarded as “slow”. He has a disability restricting and affecting his physical movement as well as his perception. He literally cannot move quickly or see things that m</span>
  <span id="freeText9617945315050853265" style="display:none">A little known and fine piece of literature is the novel Die Entdeckung der Langsamkeit (The Discovery of Slowness), by Sten Nadolny. The story is a fictionalized account of John Franklin, a historical explorer around the turn of the 19th century. As the protagonist, John Franklin is the most unlikely of adventurers because he is regarded as “slow”. He has a disability restricting and affecting his physical movement as well as his perception. He literally cannot move quickly or see things that move too quickly. Because John Franklin is slow, he cannot play at sports because he cannot see a ball coming. It is as if he sees things in slow motion. He speaks and reads slowly - aggravating those around him for what they consider mental retardation or dim-wittedness.<br />	The narrative is told through the eyes of the main character starting in his youth and progressing to his eventual promotion to captain of a polar expedition vessel looking for the Northwest Passage. Contrary to all expectations, the advantage that this disability affords Franklin is the detail he is aware of and his prodigious memory that allows him to notice changes on a micro level. The recognition of this ability by a doctor allows Franklin to compensate for his disability in ways that impact the world around him. He can visualize the consequences of certain actions in detail. One related incident involves Franklin saving his crew by his patient deliberation when his ship becomes ice-bound on a polar expedition and when the rest of the crew panic. The disadvantages of Franklin’s slowness are reflected by the repulsion and taunting he experiences from others for his disability. However, during the novel it becomes evident that this “disability” and the ways in which he compensates for it – by becoming very astute at perceiving the detail – enables Franklin to see answers to challenges that others cannot. His disability forces him to be patient until his brain catches up with the visual information he is presented with and this allows him to conceptualize the world in a unique way. <br />	The paradigmatic shifts within the novel are emphasized not only in the character’s thought but also in the way in which the novel was written and the words chosen. The author is able to simulate in words a slow way of thinking, so that when you read (at least in the German this was so) your reading rhythm becomes slower and more deliberative. You are lead to your own shift in the ability to understand how this particular way of seeing and understanding changes how the surrounding world is experienced. The superficial recounting of the life events of John Franklin remains factual, while the historical character’s inner life is fictionalized. The conceptualizations within the novel challenge social and cultural assumptions of the reader toward ability vs. disability, normal vs. abnormal, or definition of an individual by categorical assumptions and hegemony of the cultural majority. The novel also addresses how a change in paradigm whether physical or psychological alters what we are able to perceive. It challenges the rigidity with which we label correct, productive or desirable qualities and outcomes leading the reader to question their own assumptions by being given a perceptual walkabout through the eyes of another. The reader does not just understand the theoretical difference of perspective taking, but actually experiences being able to perceive in a way foreign to them by the unique way in which the novel was constructed.<br />	Nadolny has created a novel that incorporates multi-perspectival thinking as a theoretical framework and challenges the norm by re-framing what is valuable in human terms.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9617945315050853265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_92341608" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92341608" />
    <a title="Steve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/164645-steve"><img alt="Steve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442938116p2/164645.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92341608?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve" href="/user/show/164645-steve">Steve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140265842" href="/book/show/943197.The_Discovery_of_Slowness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/164645-steve?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/164645-steve?shelf=translations">translations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/164645-steve?shelf=arctic-antarctic">arctic-antarctic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92341608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14509106641219340865"><i>The Discovery of Slowness</i> is a "novel of ideas," but rather than the negative connotation that term often seems to carry, I intend it here as high praise. Nadolny's probing questions about what qualities make a person succeed or fail, and about the value of slow, determined strength, are engrossing and provocative. Those questions are made crucial to the vivid telling of John Franklin's story (the historical accuracy of which I can't speak to, but it certainly felt believable to me), so they don</span>
  <span id="freeText14509106641219340865" style="display:none"><i>The Discovery of Slowness</i> is a "novel of ideas," but rather than the negative connotation that term often seems to carry, I intend it here as high praise. Nadolny's probing questions about what qualities make a person succeed or fail, and about the value of slow, determined strength, are engrossing and provocative. Those questions are made crucial to the vivid telling of John Franklin's story (the historical accuracy of which I can't speak to, but it certainly felt believable to me), so they don't feel like abstract conjecture but vital, immediate concerns. It would be easy to reduce the story to a simple moral or metaphor, but the richness of the telling resists that. I paused often to savor an impressive sentence or to think about an intriguing idea, but it was always the story that pulled me forward and kept me engrossed (well, and the fact that I'm a sucker for anything Arctic).</span>
  <a data-text-id="14509106641219340865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_204688127" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204688127" />
    <a title="Zeb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6187834-zeb"><img alt="Zeb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322908989p2/6187834.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204688127?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zeb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zeb" href="/user/show/6187834-zeb">Zeb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">All my friends</span></div>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Zeb by: </span>
      the title jumped out at me
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6187834-zeb?shelf=europe">europe</a>,

  <span id="freeText6370401349600020054" style="display:none">One of the highlights of my life: having smoked-salmon breakfast in my house with Sten Nadolny. <div id="review_1409151419" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409151419" />
    <a title="Vira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23687480-vira"><img alt="Vira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567325844p2/23687480.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409151419?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vira" href="/user/show/23687480-vira">Vira</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781589880245" href="/book/show/26098.The_Discovery_of_Slowness">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Vira by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/15410170-asaf-bartov">Asaf Bartov</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409151419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9792198928398114280">Wonderful story! I'm too glad of having read it to tell you how exactly glad I am :) <br/><br/>Historical prose has never been my favourite genre because of its being defined — in reality a storyteller can't change the end as it had already happened. The same is true for historical fiction: what right a storyteller has, even in a book, to change the end as it had already happened? So pure fiction remains the sea I like to swim in.<br/><br/>Nevertheless, <i>The Discovery of Slowness</i> is a life story of a man I didn't kn</span>
  <span id="freeText9792198928398114280" style="display:none">Wonderful story! I'm too glad of having read it to tell you how exactly glad I am :) <br /><br />Historical prose has never been my favourite genre because of its being defined — in reality a storyteller can't change the end as it had already happened. The same is true for historical fiction: what right a storyteller has, even in a book, to change the end as it had already happened? So pure fiction remains the sea I like to swim in.<br /><br />Nevertheless, <i>The Discovery of Slowness</i> is a life story of a man I didn't know much about (ok, whom am I lying to? I didn't know anything about the named, shame on me, the geographer), thus it was same as any other fiction for me — I had no idea about the end of the story. I've caught with an eye somewhere that there was an expedition John Franklin hadn't returned from — and I haven't even once consulted Wikipedia about this :)<br /><br />Well, John Franklin made himself, long way from a child that most other children laughed at to the governor of Tasmania, not to speak of numerous titles and honours. "A man who ate his boots" but who, being a captain, always made all possible for his crew. That is how respect is gained.<br /><br />Numerous wise thoughts are pointed on here and there in the text. The one really important lies as its background: one should be slow enough not to loose time. Stuck in chasing quick events one can easily miss the slow ones, usually more useful. And speaking about governing, single person just can't watch quick and slow problems at the same time so there should be two persons in duty. The last idea alone is interesting enough for a separate book (and it surely exists for long now). Everyone has to find their own pace, own velocity, own slowness. <br /><br />If only the world were not running so blindly…<br /><br />I refused from using dictionary this time and beg the author to pardon me for omitting parts of sentences I didn't understand. I was too comforted with the narrative and its language to bother about words. A bit frightened of the book at the beginning (I expected it to be hard to comprehend), soon enough I was ashamed of my thoughts and now I would recommend the book to any of my friends. Except for the quickest ones :)<br /><br />This book came to me from Asaf who said that since I had had so much interest in the article of (and about) an autistic person, then <i>The Discovery of Slowness</i> would be no less interesting. Sure, this came true. I can't state that John Franklin was on the autistic spectrum (I'm not an expert for that). But his story of life might be of use for people who really are.<br /><br />What a pleasure to read a recommended book and to find it splendid! And to become sure once more that not only people recommend books but also vice versa.<br /><br />PS. I told myself (still afraid at the beginning): you can make it! 300 pages roughly equals to one month — ten pages a day are something real. But that was long ago. I'm laughing now because it took me <i>exactly</i> month — from October 5 to November 5 :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="9792198928398114280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1942384562" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Harinarayan Sreenivasan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43249862-harinarayan-sreenivasan"><img alt="Harinarayan Sreenivasan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498141678p2/43249862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1942384562?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Harinarayan Sreenivasan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Harinarayan Sreenivasan" href="/user/show/43249862-harinarayan-sreenivasan">Harinarayan Sreenivasan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19479499-the-discovery-of-slowness">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1942384562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7000706794116230283">This is a fictionalized biography of the 19th century Arctic explorer, Sir John Franklin. He is slow. Slowness here has nothing to do with stupidity or mental retardation. He just takes his own time to do anything and hardly gives up. Thus he turns around an apparent weakness to his greatest strength. He shows that slowness in even desired in some pursuits. Was Franklin was slow in his real life? Probably yes. Probably no. <br/><br/>This book is very popular in the artistic circles. Probably due to the fi</span>
  <span id="freeText7000706794116230283" style="display:none">This is a fictionalized biography of the 19th century Arctic explorer, Sir John Franklin. He is slow. Slowness here has nothing to do with stupidity or mental retardation. He just takes his own time to do anything and hardly gives up. Thus he turns around an apparent weakness to his greatest strength. He shows that slowness in even desired in some pursuits. Was Franklin was slow in his real life? Probably yes. Probably no. <br /><br />This book is very popular in the artistic circles. Probably due to the first part where Franklin is in his young years and is a misfit, through and through. He has his own way of looking at this world. The book is full of details, important as well as superfluous. Probably to make the reader feel the way a slow person would sense the world. And this makes the narration very different from usual novels. Second part of the book is painfully slow to read, but sets the stage for a very interesting third part. It is a very unique novel, both in its theme and narrative style and there are a few profound paragraphs worthy of rumination.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7000706794116230283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2289132129" />
    <a title="Liam Heneghan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14324851-liam-heneghan"><img alt="Liam Heneghan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352223609p2/14324851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2289132129?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liam Heneghan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liam Heneghan" href="/user/show/14324851-liam-heneghan">Liam Heneghan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781589880245" href="/book/show/26098.The_Discovery_of_Slowness">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2289132129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4438377643791341661">This novel is exceptional. Absorbing, thought-provoking, and evocative of the era (nineteenth-century) in which its British explorer protagonist, Sir John Franklin, lived. It is--perhaps this is a warning--performatively slow. It is not a page-turner understood as a rapid and thrilling read. Rather, it promotes deliberation, thoughtfulness, moments (long moments) of reverie. This may very much be your cuppa tea: it was mine. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer804078765" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10186918466045641540">This book is brilliant though not always fun to read. This shouldn't be surprising because it is about slowness and it makes you feel Franklin's slowness, the great strength and also the initial handicap that results from it as well his great patience and wisdom, all of which would not be possible without his slowness. Nadolny also does a great job at portraying the social environment that often confronts Franklin with mockery and contempt for his slowness, but over time learns to acknowledge an</span>
  <span id="freeText10186918466045641540" style="display:none">This book is brilliant though not always fun to read. This shouldn't be surprising because it is about slowness and it makes you feel Franklin's slowness, the great strength and also the initial handicap that results from it as well his great patience and wisdom, all of which would not be possible without his slowness. Nadolny also does a great job at portraying the social environment that often confronts Franklin with mockery and contempt for his slowness, but over time learns to acknowledge and appreciate his great talent, complete with the political, ideological and technological changes that transform this environment during Franklin's lifetime. The book also makes it easy to re-imagine the various settings of the book: rural England, where Franklin grew up, London, the Royal Navy at war, the Arctic, and Tasmania. All of these aspects together make this a great and enlightening read, which I highly recommend. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17845377665273698543">This book is about polar explorer John Franklin -- on the surface. But it is really about seeing the world differently than most, perhaps what would now be called being neuro-atypical. <br/><br/>What I found most impressive about this book was the slowness of its prose. Not tedious or boring, but slow. The rhythm of its sentences, the pacing of the narrative: slow. Slow in its pure, not perjorative sense. To convey this is also a masterwork of translation.<br/><br/>The narrative covers the first of Franklin's polar</span>
  <span id="freeText17845377665273698543" style="display:none">This book is about polar explorer John Franklin -- on the surface. But it is really about seeing the world differently than most, perhaps what would now be called being neuro-atypical. <br /><br />What I found most impressive about this book was the slowness of its prose. Not tedious or boring, but slow. The rhythm of its sentences, the pacing of the narrative: slow. Slow in its pure, not perjorative sense. To convey this is also a masterwork of translation.<br /><br />The narrative covers the first of Franklin's polar expeditions at length but not so much the last one (the ships had not yet been found). There's a good deal on his childhood and service in the Napoleonic wars, and a chapter on his governorship of Tasmania and his largely unrealized efforts to humanize the penal colony.</span>

<div id="review_2848158938" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2848158938" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27986103-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441940772p2/27986103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2848158938?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/27986103-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781589880245" href="/book/show/26098.The_Discovery_of_Slowness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27986103-mike?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2848158938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14503343613656182448">This book, which first appeared in 1983, and has been translated into many languages, has now been re-issued - with some updating of Ralph Freedman’s superb translation.<br/><br/>It’s a fictionalised biography of John Franklin, and also a meditation on perseverance, difference, and the way in which time is perceived. Franklin first went to sea as a boy and had a long career both in the Navy – he was at the Battle of Trafalgar – and later as an explorer in the Arctic seas. <br/><br/>The book is regarded as Nadolny’s</span>
  <span id="freeText14503343613656182448" style="display:none">This book, which first appeared in 1983, and has been translated into many languages, has now been re-issued - with some updating of Ralph Freedman’s superb translation.<br /><br />It’s a fictionalised biography of John Franklin, and also a meditation on perseverance, difference, and the way in which time is perceived. Franklin first went to sea as a boy and had a long career both in the Navy – he was at the Battle of Trafalgar – and later as an explorer in the Arctic seas. <br /><br />The book is regarded as Nadolny’s masterpiece, and certainly engages the reader in an entirely different world. We’re forced to see the world through Franklin’s eyes: he was a man who perceived things at a slower speed than the average human being, and who had to study harder than most, and memorise and learn the particularities of other people’s speech and behaviour, in order to live in ordinary society. <br /><br />Nadolny’s achievement is to stretch out events in such a way that we see the detail as Franklin did and feel the depth of his struggles. The book is packed with characters, many of whom appear only for a page or two, floating past Franklin’s perception and often making little impact on the reader. It’s necessary to come to the book prepared to go with its unusual pace, and inhabit the world as Franklin did; to read it as a ‘novel’ may be a dissatisfying experience. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14503343613656182448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/1416715-donna">Donna</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781589880245" href="/book/show/26098.The_Discovery_of_Slowness">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2837289108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11783665784004131935">This is the most satisfying and well written book I have come across this year. The book is ostensibly about John Franklin the explorer, but it is so much more. As a child he was slow and probably today would be considered to have learning disabilities or be labelled on the autism spectrum. He managed to understand his own personal rhythm in life, and he had discovered coping mechanisms to deal with what he faced in order to pursue a life in the British navy. The book is beautifully constructed </span>
  <span id="freeText11783665784004131935" style="display:none">This is the most satisfying and well written book I have come across this year. The book is ostensibly about John Franklin the explorer, but it is so much more. As a child he was slow and probably today would be considered to have learning disabilities or be labelled on the autism spectrum. He managed to understand his own personal rhythm in life, and he had discovered coping mechanisms to deal with what he faced in order to pursue a life in the British navy. The book is beautifully constructed and well written. Thru the writing, the author manages to convey Franklin's sense of slowness. There is also a lot to learn about the advantages of slowing down. It also has a lot to say about accepting and cultivating our differences and using them to our advantage. Highly recommend.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11783665784004131935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText2068470532065107625" style="display:none">A fictionalized biography of Artic explorer John Franklin. The first thing we are told about Franklin is that he is slow. And his Slowness is what gives him the iron will to carry on and follow his dreams. The narration is meant to make us see how Franklin would see the world: full of details and sometimes unrelated thoughts. There are a few scenes, especially the ones with action, that make you realize how fast we are living and how we lose focus on what surrounds. It made me realize how anxious sometimes I am about losing an opportunity or a moment, when probably in reality not rushing and taking it slow would make actually make me live the moment and make better decisions, towards what one truly wants and dreams.<br />Highly recommend.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17684539597265385694">Unusual biography based on the life of 19th century explorer Sir John Franklin, who became a hero during the Battle of Trafalgar. Promoted to ship's captain in the Royal Navy, Franklin led an expedition in search of the Northwest Passage. He and his crew barely survived the journey; most perished from cold or starvation. As a young man, many mistook Franklin's intentionally slow, deliberate manner for stupidity, but it was these very qualities that made him a successful ship commander and expedi</span>
  <span id="freeText17684539597265385694" style="display:none">Unusual biography based on the life of 19th century explorer Sir John Franklin, who became a hero during the Battle of Trafalgar. Promoted to ship's captain in the Royal Navy, Franklin led an expedition in search of the Northwest Passage. He and his crew barely survived the journey; most perished from cold or starvation. As a young man, many mistook Franklin's intentionally slow, deliberate manner for stupidity, but it was these very qualities that made him a successful ship commander and expedition leader. <br /><br />This book should appeal especially to those who enjoy stories about sea-faring life and 19th century military history. The attention to detail in describing his crews, his ships and the challenges of commanding a military vessel makes this an above-average adventure story. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5477583261853667167">Author Sten Nadolny has imagined a background for John Franklin in which the seeming impediment which makes his childhood miserable is the very thing that eventually makes him an ideal Arctic explorer. Franklin can only perceive the world slowly and with great deliberation. This puts him out of pace with most of the world, leading him to be labeled as slow and stupid. It is only with the help of an astute teacher, and his own resolve and obstinacy, that he learns to work with his atypical intell</span>
  <span id="freeText5477583261853667167" style="display:none">Author Sten Nadolny has imagined a background for John Franklin in which the seeming impediment which makes his childhood miserable is the very thing that eventually makes him an ideal Arctic explorer. Franklin can only perceive the world slowly and with great deliberation. This puts him out of pace with most of the world, leading him to be labeled as slow and stupid. It is only with the help of an astute teacher, and his own resolve and obstinacy, that he learns to work with his atypical intelligence.<br /><br />The pace of the opening chapters is, as you might expect, slow, but patient readers will be rewarded with a fascinating exploration of perception, time, and psychology.</span>

<div id="review_3125096610" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lepe Parviainen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lepe Parviainen" href="/user/show/6248314-lepe-parviainen">Lepe Parviainen</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3125096610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3508958535621389536">An enjoyable, partly fictionalised biography of the great British explorer of the Arctic, sir John Franklin (1786–1847). The book takes you back 200 years to the Arctic Sea, Tasmanian colony, London and the Northwest Passage in Northern Canada. The key concept of the book is that Franklin is painted as a mentally slow person, who might be diagnosed today having a neuropsychiatric disorder. This quality is celebrated and praised despite the hardships it brings him.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3230287848" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3230287848" />
    <a title="Klaas Bischoff" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/109339705-klaas-bischoff"><img alt="Klaas Bischoff" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580984129p2/109339705.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Klaas Bischoff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Klaas Bischoff" href="/user/show/109339705-klaas-bischoff">Klaas Bischoff</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3230287848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10422072449113801512">Nadolny tells the story of the British explorer Sir John Franklin, who lived in the 18th and 19th century. Franklin has always been slower with everything compared to his peers. This books tells the story of a man who used his slowness to his advantage and became a successful captain whose goal it was to find the Northwest Passage. <br/><br/>The book contains some interesting life lessons related to taking one's time. The story itself, however, I did not find very entertaining. </span>

<div id="review_3076381235" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3076381235" />
    <a title="Hưng Bùi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44816275-h-ng-b-i"><img alt="Hưng Bùi" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3076381235?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hưng Bùi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hưng Bùi" href="/user/show/44816275-h-ng-b-i">Hưng Bùi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781589880245" href="/book/show/26098.The_Discovery_of_Slowness">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3076381235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4161129939011170623">In accordance with the name, the book starts very slowly and bordering on boring, which almost prompts me to drop it. It also does not help with a somewhat peculiar prose which is hard to follow at first. But you get used to it. Fortunately the pace picks up later. The book isn't so much about slowness and its significance but more about Sir John Franklin life and exploration, which are indeed interesting. The author's narration contains stuff worth contemplating imo.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2141825701" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2141825701" />
    <a title="Lauren Mangold" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4100770-lauren-mangold"><img alt="Lauren Mangold" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500229949p2/4100770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2141825701?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren Mangold" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren Mangold" href="/user/show/4100770-lauren-mangold">Lauren Mangold</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781589880245" href="/book/show/26098.The_Discovery_of_Slowness">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2141825701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15874100066236097692">Nadolny uses the real life and exploits of the historical John Franklin to frame a narrative both absorbing and epistemological. When he composed the work in German in 1983, 'neurodiversity' was hardly the watchword it has become today, and yet the author makes clear the virtues of Franklin's "slowness".</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2212263298" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2212263298" />
    <a title="Colin Murphy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27185146-colin-murphy"><img alt="Colin Murphy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520362025p2/27185146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2212263298?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Colin Murphy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Colin Murphy" href="/user/show/27185146-colin-murphy">Colin Murphy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19856492-the-discovery-of-slowness">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2212263298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6092849741681861087">The problem with such a book being crafted 150 years after the actual man lived is that it becomes too heavily entrenched in the contemporary norms of a hero. These implausible virtues for a man of Franklin's era distracted from what this book is so beautifully centered around: slowness. The deluge of morality added nothing given the fact that slowness can clearly benefit the bad as well.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CcCGhZh6ceD2oneHPGL1nk3RVwMSVxYMc3iLlFvsqXof1OAe4EmgS8RV75jhFSkE+VidHLzBdvhhzTal26ZqTg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gUgOBzIyxmgKX/DamKvgmTwQokpOjxS1LEMY8Q0c8heXXGicSgEXwzioaMVF3DwDiJloVeAZdEE+9qXAjVYxIw==')})
  }

Karo mit ihrem mittelmäßigen Freund, den sie verlässt. Karo heulend am Telefon, um ihren Freund, den sie nicht will, (erfolglos) zurückzubekommen. Karo ohne Freund heulend in den Armen – und auf den Knien – ihres besten Freundes. Karo heulend in der Psychiatrie. Und, am Ende, dann doch: Alles wieder gut. Aber auch Kuttners Roman hat Schwächen, und die haben eben mit der psychologischen Ausgestaltung der Hauptfigur zu tun. Denn Karo ist zwar sympathisch und chaotisch, aber sie hat nicht das mindeste Geheimnis mehr. Alles über ihr Wesen wird in der Ich-Perspektive durch Selbstreflexionen aufgeschlüsselt, nichts entwickelt sich aus der Geschichte selbst. So will man als Psychiater im offenen Buch einer Patientin lesen. Aber von einem Roman erwartet man als Leser schon ein bisschen mehr.\n\nVielleicht ist dieses &quot;mehr&quot; aber gar nicht so wichtig. Denn Karo ist eine kluge, witzige, beizeiten auch selbstironische junge Frau, und Kuttner ist eine mindestens ebenso kluge und witzige wie genaue Beobachterin der kleinen Schwächen postmoderner Menschen um die Dreißig. Das findet sich auch im Duktus von Mängelexemplar wieder – etwa da, wo er die anglizismisierte Computersprache (gedownloaded) in die Beschreibung eines Abendessens (&quot;geabendbrotet&quot;) transformiert. So sollte man Mängelexemplar trotz aller Mängel trotzdem lesen.             e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_6334076').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12431238942493702152">Sten Nadolny, (born 29 July 1942, in Zehdenick, Province of Brandenburg) is a German novelist. His parents, Burkhard and Isabella Nadolny, were also writers.<br/><br/>His best known work is "The Discovery of Slowness" (1987; originally published in 1983 as "Die Entdeckung der Langsamkeit"), a fictionalized meditation on the life and lessons of British Arctic explorer Sir John Franklin. A pre-publication por</span>
  <span id="freeText12431238942493702152" style="display:none">Sten Nadolny, (born 29 July 1942, in Zehdenick, Province of Brandenburg) is a German novelist. His parents, Burkhard and Isabella Nadolny, were also writers.<br /><br />His best known work is "The Discovery of Slowness" (1987; originally published in 1983 as "Die Entdeckung der Langsamkeit"), a fictionalized meditation on the life and lessons of British Arctic explorer Sir John Franklin. A pre-publication portion of the novel titled "Kopenhagen 1801" (which would become the fifth chapter) had earned Nadolny the Ingeborg Bachmann Prize in 1980.</span>
